Fitzjocelyn having say his say, it be his turn and his nature to be

talk down.



'in short,' conclude James, walk about the room, 'there be no

alternative.  wait for a College living be bad enough, but nothing

else can make happiness even possible.'



'one would think you mean one sort of happiness,' say Louis, with a

calm consider tone, and look of inquiry which James could not brook.



'what else?' he cry.  'Fool and madman that I be to dwell on the

hopeless--'



'why should it be hopeless?--' begin Louis.



'Hush! you be the last person with whom I could discuss this subject,'

bear my burthen alone.  believe I, I struggle hard. if you and I be

destine to clash, one comfort be, that even I could never quarrel with

'I have not the remotest idea of your meaning.'



'so much the well.  no, so much the bad.  you be not capable of

feel what I do for she, or you would have hate I long ago.  do not

don't let I lose you, Louis.'



James wring the hand of his cousin; and no soon be he alone, than he

'Poor Jem!' soliloquize Fitzjocelyn.  'at least, I be glad the trouble

be love, not the ordination.  but as to his meaning!  he give I to

no clash there--! Nay, the other it can never be--after all his

might have be a first, but for his past waste of time.



he be sorry to leave Oxford: he have be happy there in his own

desultory fashion; and the additional time that his illness have keep

he be to go to join his father in London; and he carry thither

it be a second youth of the affection, but it be purchase by a step

credit to satisfy his father.



'Oakstead be talk it over with I,' be the answer; 'and we

themselves.'

never have devise such consolation.'



'perhaps the exclusive devotion to study which attain higher honour

'it be do the immediate work with the whole might.'



'you do work with all your might.'



'ay! but too many iron in the fire, and none of they red-hot through,

'materially bad?'

'thank you; but I be sure you cannot wish to go out after such news.'



'there be not sufficient excuse for refuse.  there be to be no party,

accord to Northwold gossip.'



'Nonsense!  Jem would scorn an heiress if she be ten time pretty.

he begin to question whether his interview with James have be a dream.

'I think I hate it more because I hate it less.'



'Translate, if you please.'



'the first half-year, I scorn they all, and they scorn I; and that

'the next, you have disturb I; I could not go on be savage with

one and a half.  the whole one be a good, rough, stupid girl, who come

colour your eye be!'



'the encounter have make you so epigrammatic and satirical, that there

'oh, dear! les voila!' cry Clara, as, enter Hanover Square, they

the evening would have be very happy, have not Lord Ormersfield look

his eye have glitter at the proposal before he recollect the sorrow

'there be a high spirit and originality about Clara, which make she a

'she must be such a riddle to her respectable school-fellow, that

look at our fade dowager here.'

'no; but he could have rob their homage of half--nay, all its grace.'

'I be sorry for you,' say he, in his peculiar tone: 'I suppose I be

the word be prompt by a keen, sudden desire to mark their effect;

'Fitzjocelyn,' say the Earl, on the way home, 'do not think it

'I have rather not, thank you,' say Louis, in an almost provokingly

'it be full time you should assume your own guidance.'



'how little he know how little that would suit he!' think Louis,

everything, and never even satisfy he?'









CHAPTER XVIII.



rest for the WEARY.



  therefore, arm thee for the strife

  all throughout this mortal life,

  soldier now and servant true,

  Earth behind, and heaven in view.

                       REV. I. WILLIAMS.





the first impression on arrive at Northwold be, that the danger have

be magnify.  Mrs. Frost's buoyant spirit have rise at the first

respite; and though there be a weight on Mary's brow, she speak

cheerfully, and as if able to attend to other interest, tell Louis

of her father's wish for some good workman to superintend the mine,

and ask he to consult his friend at Illershall on the subject.



Lord Ormersfield come down encourage by his visit to the invalid, whom

he have find dressed and able to converse nearly as usual.  she beg

promise with a smile that if he would bring Louis, their aunt should

chaperon Mary.



when the Earl go upstairs after dinner, the other three close round

the fire, and talk in a tranquil, subdue strain, on various topic,

sometimes grave, sometimes enliven by the playfulness inherent in two

yet it be less the matter than the manner of their dialogue--the deep,

'thank you, I never be so comfortable, not even when my foot be bad.'

day, would probably be the last.



'do Mary know?'



'she do.  she bear up nobly.'



'and what be to become of she?'



the Earl sigh deeply.  'Lima be her destiny.  her mother be bent on

it, and say that she wish it herself; but on one thing I be

'her word--almost her word,' say the Earl, between earnestness and

past I how such saying be a consolation.'



'not if they be no more than saying.'



there be silence.  Louis hear an occasional groaning sigh from his

one of his sudden and impetuous resolution.



the next morning, he order his horse, say he would bring the last

report from the Terrace.

not hesitate, but slowly, almost inaudibly, she bring out the

'I do.  I trust your principle and kindness implicitly, but I think the

'it be very hard,' say Louis; 'every one will have it that I must be

in love, till I shall have to believe so myself, and when I know it

'you be make yourself more simple than you really be,' say Mra.

Ponsonby, half provoke.



Louis shut his eye, and seem to be rouse his faculty; then,

'Distaste--and rather a taste for be quiz,' say Louis.

'my father will have I walk in no line but his own.'



'you have sense not to make duty to he an excuse for indolence and

'I don't know what to do!' say Louis.  'when I think the aim of my

'it will be a disappointment to he, if you do not act and decide for

'on the contrary,' exclaim Louia, indignantly, 'all the resolution I

ever show come from nothing else!'



'I know it.  let he see that these thing make a man of you; and,

Louis--you feel what a difference it might make!'



Louis bow his head thoughtfully.



'you, who be both son and daughter to he, may give up scheme and

pleasure for his sake, and may undertake work for which you have no

natural turn; but, however you may cross your inclination, never be

'perseverance--your old lesson.'



'yes; you must learn to work over the moment when novelty be go and

'my poor private judgment! you work it hard! when it have generally only

run I full-drive into some egregious blunder!'



'not your true deliberate judgment, exercise with a sense of

responsibility.  Humility must not cover your laziness.  you have such

quality and such talent as must be intend to do good to other,

not to be trifle away in fitful exertion.  make it your great effort

to see clearly, and then to proceed steadfastly, without slacken

'and you willn't let I have the one person who can see clearly, and keep

I steady?'



'to be your husband, instead of your wife!  no, Louis; you must learn

to take yourself on your own hand, and lean neither on your father,

nor on any one else on earth, before you can be fit for Mary, or--'



'and if I do?' begin Louis.



'you would make a man of yourself,' she say, interrupt he. 'that

be the first thing--not a reed shake with the wind.  you can do it;

there be nothing that Grace cannot do.'



'I know there be not,' say Louis, reverently.



'and, oh! the blessing that you would so bring on yourself and on your

Louis's heart be too full to make any answer.  Mrs. Ponsonby lie back

Louis knelt on one knee beside she, hold her hand, and bow down his

he go down stair, and out of the house, and take his horse from the

Mary come home; and if she know why that long walk have be urge on

Mary come, and her mother take both her hand.  they be chilly; and

there be a little pulse on Mary's temple that visibly throb, and

almost seem to leap, with fearful rapidity.

you in suspense.  I be afraid it will not do.'

CHAPTER XIX.



MOONSHINE.



  he talk of dagger and of dart,

    of passion and of pain,

  of weep eye and wound heart,

    of kiss and of chain:

  but still the lady shake her head,

    and swear by yea and nay,

  my whole be all that he have say,

    and all that he could say.

                     W. MACKWORTH PRAED.

the poor old furniture at Ormersfield!

the village girl, hard press, be break out.

conflict for liberty, where the desperate poniard be uplifted--there--'



'oh! don't talk so dreadful.  Pray--'



'do you bid I pause?  at a word from you.  you be the arbitress of my

'no; I've nothing to do--do go!  only promise you'll not do nothing

dangerous--'



'reject I, and life be intolerable.  where the madden crowd rise

'you'll be the first to take to your heel, I'll be bind!  ben't you

fashion?' cry the friendly dragon Martha, descend on they.

'that I do! and richly you deserve it, too, sir!  see if your missus

the 'sex' fairly scold the courteous Delaford off the field; and

Jane comfort she; Martha hold that he be the last man in the world

in the meantime, Fitzjocelyn have begin with a fit of bashfulness. the

this wear off quickly; the new scene take effect on his impressible

people, and not at all of each other.



only Isabel think she would make the Viscount into a Vidame, both as

need approval of his theory in Mary's eye, crave Mary's

sympathy, follow she on her voyage, and imagine her arrival.

be it the perverse spirit of longing after the most unattainable?



he demand of himself whether it be a fatal sign that he regret

the loss of Isabel, when she go to spend a few day with her old

care of the motherless child of a good-for-nothing brother, who have

education for her niece, which detain she at Paris; and as she have a

member, yet it be not the loss of the sun; and that he be quite as

ready to tease his aunt and make Virginia laugh, as if Isabel have be

look on with a smile of wonder and commiseration for their nonsense.









CHAPTER XX.



the FANTASTIC VISCOUNT.

outside the door he find Delaford, who beg to suggest to his

he think there be sign bode tempest.  shop be closed, and man

the dark blue group be thicken into crowd; musket and pike

a discovery break on, he.  well that he could bear it!

grim look be level at they by the fierce black-bearded man, and

his perfidious tongue as it may.'



'there's my answer,' say Louis, raise his right arm, which be

'ha!' cry the friendly fishwife, 'wound in the cause of the nation!

let he go.'



'he have not utter the cry!' shout the rest.



Louis look round with his cool, pensive smile.



'Liberty!' he say, 'what _we_ mean by liberty be freedom to go where

we will, and say what we will.  I wish you have it, my poor fellow.

Fraternity--it be not shoot our brother.  Egalite--I preach that

too, but in my own fashion, not your.  let I pass--si cela vou est

egal.'



his nonchalant intrepidity--a quality never lose on the French--raise

the troop be re-form after the repulse, and the point be to pass

'oh no, no; but you--'

'oh, Fitzjocelyn!' she scream, 'tell he so--tell he to take we to

Isabel look up and smile, as Louis stand by she, leave his aunt

lady have a curious pseudo presence of mind.'



'generally, I believe,' say Isabel, 'a woman's presence of mind should

Isabel readily fall into the same strain.  'they turn from daylight

and follow the glare of their own gas,' say she.



so they begin a backward tracing of the calamity of France; and, as

the Captain have profit sufficiently by the Sister's example to be

CHAPTER XXI.



the HERO of the barricade.



  the page slay the boar,

  the peer have the gloire.

               Quentin Durward.

Pendragon?' run this off with calm, slow, impressive deliberation.

oh, vanity! vanity! how many garb dost thou wear!

'Jem!  Jem! have you hear?'

and Co. swell the majority as soon as they see that their friend have

no chance.



Poor Mr. Powell go home to his drudgery with his wrinkle deeply than

ever; and his wife sigh as she resign her last hope of send she

son to the University.



Mr. Calcott have, for the first time in his life, be over-ridden by an

unscrupulous use of his neighbour's rank; and of the youthfulness that

inspire hope of fix a claim on an untried, inexperienced man.



the old squire be severely hurt and mortify; but he be very

magnanimous--generously wish James joy, and congratulate Mrs. Frost

with all his heart.  he be less cordial with Louis; but the bad he

say of he be, that he be but a lad, his father be out of the way,

and he wish he might not find that he have get himself into a scrape.

he could not think why a man of old Ormersfield's age should go

figure round Cape Horn, instead of stay to keep his own son in

order.



Sydney be absent; but the rest of the family and their friend be

less forbearing than the person chiefly concerned.  they talk

furiously, and make a strong exertion of forgiveness in order not to

cut Fitzjocelyn.  Sir Gilbert Brewster vow that it would serve he

right to be turn out of the troop, and that he must keep a sharp look

out lest he should sow disaffection among the Yeomanry.  make friend

with Ramsbotham! never take out a gun!  the country be go to the

dog when such as he be to be a peer!
